Sale of Wine is Void in Hanafi Fiqh
States a ruling on the invalidity of selling wine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling wine and explain why it is classified as batil rather than fasid.

Core Idea
Wine is not property (mal), so its sale is void ab initio — batil, not merely fasid.

This lesson examines a fundamental ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the sale of wine is absolutely void. Understanding this requires grasping the concept of mal mutaqawwim (property eligible for trade). Wine, being impure and prohibited, lacks this status, making any transaction in it legally null.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The source says 'The sale of wine is void.' The Arabic term is 'batil'. This is the strongest level of invalidity.
Batil means the contract has no legal effect whatsoever.
2
Understand the basis
In Hanafi fiqh, a valid sale requires the object to be mal mutaqawwim. Wine is not considered property because it is intrinsically impure and forbidden for consumption.
Mal mutaqawwim: valuable property that is permissible to benefit from.
3
Distinguish from other categories
If a sale is void due to a missing element in the object itself, it is batil. If the defect is in the contract formation (e.g., unknown price), it is fasid.
Fasid contracts can become valid by removing the defect; batil cannot.
4
Apply the ruling
Thus, any transaction involving wine – selling, buying, or even gifting – is null. Ownership does not transfer, and any payment is unlawful.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Other schools (e.g., Hanbali) may allow selling wine to non-Muslims under certain conditions, but Hanafi holds it absolutely batil.
The Hanafi view is based on the Quran and hadith prohibiting khamr in all forms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹی بحث شراب کی بیع باطل ہے
The sixth discussion: The sale of wine is void.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the table of contents of Ashraf al-Hidayah, indicating the Hanafi position that the sale of wine (khamr) is invalid (batil). The discussion likely falls under the section on forbidden sales. In the Hanafi school, wine is not considered property (mal) because it is intrinsically impure and prohibited, hence any transaction involving it is void ab initio.

Key Terms
شراب (sharab): Intoxicating beverage, specifically wine (khamr) in this context.
باطل (batil): Void, no legal effect; the contract is null from the start.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Property that is legally valuable and permissible to use; a condition for valid sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi ruling on the sale of wine?
A) Permissible if sold to non-Muslims
B) Makruh tahrimi
C) Batil (void)
D) Fasid (irregular)

Key Takeaway
The sale of wine is void (batil) in the Hanafi school because wine is not considered mal mutaqawwim.

Constitution and Perfection of Rahn
Opening ruling on rahn: formation and perfection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two stages of the contract of rahn and identify the condition required for it to become binding.

Core Idea
A rahn contract is formed by offer and acceptance but becomes binding only upon possession.

This passage introduces the fundamental Hanafi ruling on the contract of rahn (pledge). It distinguishes between the constitution of the contract (in'iqad) and its perfection (tamam). Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines when the creditor's right to hold the property becomes enforceable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two elements of contract formation
The ruling states that rahn is concluded (mun'aqid) by ijab (offer) and qabul (acceptance). These two elements create a valid contract.
Offer and acceptance are common to all contracts in Islamic law.
2
Identify the element that perfects the contract
The contract is perfected (tamm) by qabd (possession). Perfection here means the contract becomes binding (lazim) and enforceable.
Until possession is taken, the contract is not fully operative.
3
Understand the legal effect of each stage
After ijab and qabul, the contract is valid (sahih) but not binding. After qabd, it becomes binding and the mortgagee has the right to hold the property as security.
The debtor can revoke the pledge before possession is taken.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam Malik holds that possession is not required for binding; the contract is binding upon offer and acceptance alone. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position emphasizes the security nature of rahn requiring actual control.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہن ایجاب و قبول سے منعقد ہوتا ہے اور قبضہ سے تام ہوتا ہے
The pledge (rahn) is concluded (mun'aqid) by offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), and is perfected (tamm) by possession (qabd).
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the basic ruling on the contract of rahn (mortgage/pledge) in Hanafi fiqh. It establishes two key stages: the contract itself is formed through the usual elements of offer and acceptance (ijab wa qabul), but it does not become fully operative (tamm) until the mortgaged property is physically delivered into the possession of the mortgagee (murtahin). Until possession is taken, the contract is not binding and the mortgagee does not have the right to hold the property as security. This ruling distinguishes between the validity of the contract (in`iqad) and its perfection (tamam), which are separate legal events. The Hanafi school holds that possession is a condition for the contract to become binding (lazim).

Key Terms
رہن (rahn): A contract whereby property is given as security for a debt; the property is held by the creditor but not owned by him.
ایجاب و قبول (ijab wa qabul): Offer and acceptance; the oral or written expression of mutual consent that forms the contract.
قبضہ (qabd): Physical possession; taking control of the mortgaged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a contract of rahn (pledge) become binding (lazim)?
A) Upon offer and acceptance alone.
B) Only after the debt falls due.
C) Only after possession (qabd) of the pledged property is taken.
D) Only after written documentation is signed.

Key Takeaway
A rahn contract is formed by ijab and qabul but is perfected only by qabd; without possession, it is not binding.

The Three-Year Waiting Period After Tahjir
Explains the ruling and proof for three-year waiting period after tahjir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the waiting period for a mutahajjir, explain its proof, and distinguish between the religious obligation (diyanatan) and legal ownership.

Core Idea
Tahjir gives priority, not ownership; the three-year waiting period is a religious guideline, not a legal condition for ownership.

In Hanafi fiqh, marking dead land (tahjir) is a step before actual revival (ihya). But how long does the marker's priority last? This lesson explains the three-year waiting period established by the practice of Umar (RA) and the rational reasoning behind it. Crucially, it clarifies that this waiting period is a matter of religious adherence (diyanatan), not a legal bar. If another person revives the land before three years, that reviver becomes the owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahjir (marking land). The ruling: a three-year waiting period is required for the marker (mutahajjir). This is a religious obligation (wajib diyanatan).
The waiting period is not a legal condition for ownership.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA): 'There is no right for the one who marks land after three years' (narrated by Qadi Abu Yusuf in Kitab al-Kharaj from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib).
This is a Qawl Sahabi, which is considered a proof in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the rational justification
The marker needs time to return to his homeland, prepare resources, and come back. Three years is estimated as sufficient: one year travel each way and one year for preparation. Shorter periods (hours, days, months) are insufficient.
This is a rational extension (qiyas) based on the general need.
4
Distinguish diyanatan from legal ownership
The three-year waiting period is a religious guideline (diyanatan). Legally, if another person revives the land before the three years pass, that second person becomes the owner because actual revival (ihya) occurred from him.
The first marker's prior claim does not prevent ownership by the reviver.
5
Note the disliked nature
It is makruh (disliked) to outbid or interfere with the marker's priority, but if a purchase occurs, the contract is valid.
This shows the ethical dimension of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانما شرط ترك ثلاث سنين لقول عمر رضى الله عنه ليس لمتحجر بعد ثلاث سنين حق ولانه اذا اعلمه لايد من زمان يرجع فيه الى وطنه وزمان يهيي اموره فيه ثم زمان يرجع الى ما يحجره فقدرناه بثلاث سنين لان مادونها من الساعات والايام والشهور لا يفى بذلك واذا لم يحضر بعد انقضائها فالظاهر انه تركها قالوا هذا كله ديانة فاما اذا احياها غيره قبل مضى هذه المدة ملكها لتحقق الاحياء منه دون الأول فصار هو ولو فعل كره ولو فعل يجوز العقد۔
ترجمہ: اور شرط لگائی مصنف نے تین سال چھوڑنے کی عمر کے قول کی وجہ سے کہ متجر کے لئے تین سال کے بعد حق نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ جب اس نے اس پر نشان لگا دیا تو اتنے زمانہ کا ہونا کہ وہ واپس آسکے اس زمین کے پاس جس کی اس نے تجھیز کی ہے۔ تو ہم نے اس کو تین سال کے ساتھ مقدر کیا اس لئے کہ جو اس سے کم ساعات اور ایام اور مہینے میں وہ اس کو چکا نہیں سکتے ( یعنی کافی ہوں گے ) اور جب وہ حاضر نہ ہوا تین سال گذرنے کے بعد تو ظاہر یہ ہے کہ اس نے اس کو چھوڑ دیا۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ یہ دیانت ہے ہیں بہر حال جبکہ اس ' کے غیر نے اس کا احیاء کر لیا اس مدت کے گذرنے سے پہلے تو وہ اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا اس کی جانب سے احیاء کے متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے نہ کہ اول کی مایسے تو ایسے ہو گیا جیسے غیر کے بھاؤ پر بھاؤ کرنا یہ مکروہ ہے اور اگر کر لیا گیا تو عقد جائز ہوگا۔
تشریح: جس نے احیاء کے لئے نشان لگایا ہے اس کا تین سال تک انتظار کیا جائے گا اس کے بعد نہیں، کیوں اس لئے کہ قاضی ابو یوسف نے کتاب الخراج میں سعید بن المسیب سے عمر فاروق کا یہ فرمان نقل کیا ہے کہ متجر کے لئے تین سال کے بعد کوئی حق نہیں۔ پھر اس پر عقلی دلیل پیش فرمائی کہ نشان لگانے کے بعد اسکو اتنا زمانہ چاہیے کہ وہ اپنے وطن میں جاسکے اور وہاں رہتے ہوئے احیاء کے اسباب فراہم کر سکے پھر وہاں سے لوٹ کر اس زمین کا احیاء کر سکے کیونکہ دارالاسلام اتنا وسیع ہے کہ اس کے ایک کونہ سے دوسرے تک وہ ایک سال میں پہنچے گا ( یعنی پیدل ) اور یہ فرض کرو کہ وہ ایک کونہ کا رہنے والا ہے اور دوسرے کونہ میں اس نے تجیر کی ہے تا کہ احیاء کر سکے تو دو سال تو آنے اور جانے کے لئے ہو گئے اور ایک سال اسباب کے فراہم کرنے میں مشغولیت میں تو تین سال ہو گئے اور تین سال سے کم کی مقدر ان جملہ امور کو انجام دینے کے لئے ناکافی ہوں گے۔ البتہ اگر وہ تین سال کے بعد بھی واپس نہیں آتا تو یہ اس کی دلیل ہوگی کہ اس نے اپنا ارادہ ترک کر دیا ہے لیکن یہ ساری گنا دیانت ہے اور باعتبار حکم بات یہ ہے کہ اگر تین سال کے گذرنے سے پہلے ہی کسی نے اس کو آباد کر لیا تو وہی اس کا مالک بن جائے گا۔ کیونکہ احیاء دوہرے نے کیا ہے نہ کہ اول نے تو یہ بالکل ایسا ہے یکے کسی بھاؤ بھاؤ کرنا مکروہ ہے لیکن اگر کر لیا اور خرید لیا تو جائز ہے۔
And the condition of leaving three years is stipulated because of the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'There is no right for the one who marks land after three years.' And because when he marks it, he needs time to return to his homeland, time to prepare his affairs, and then time to return to what he marked. So we estimated it as three years, because less than that from hours, days, and months is insufficient for that. And when he does not appear after its expiration, apparently he has abandoned it. They said: All this is religiously (diyanatan). As for if someone else revives it before the passing of this period, he owns it due to the actualization of revival from him and not from the first. So it becomes like when one does it, it is disliked, but if he does it, the contract is valid.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the waiting period for a person who marks dead land (tahjir) with the intention of reviving it. The text states that a three-year waiting period is required based on the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) reported by Qadi Abu Yusuf in Kitab al-Kharaj, relayed through Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib. The rational proof is that after marking, the person needs time to travel to his home (possibly up to a year each way in the vast Islamic state) and a year to gather resources for revival, totalling three years. Periods shorter than this (hours, days, months) are insufficient. If the person does not appear after three years, it is presumed he has abandoned his intention. However, the text clarifies that this waiting period is a matter of religious guidance (diyanatan) and not a legal condition for ownership. Legally, if someone else revives the land even before the three years have passed, that second person becomes the owner because actual revival (ihya) has occurred from him, not from the first marker. The first marker's prior claim does not prevent ownership by the reviver, though it is disliked (makruh) to outbid or interfere in this manner. If the first marker later purchases the land from the reviver, the sale is valid.

Key Terms
تحجير (tahjīr): Marking land with stones or other signs to indicate a claim of intended revival.
متحجر (mutahajjir): A person who marks land (tahjir) for the purpose of later reviving it.
إحياء الموات (iḥyāʾ al-mawāt): Reviving dead land by making it cultivable or usable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal consequence if a second person revives dead land that was previously marked by another, before the three-year waiting period has expired?
A) The second person does not become the owner because the first marker's right is absolute.
B) The second person becomes the owner because actual revival occurred from him, and the first marker's claim does not prevent ownership.
C) The land becomes disputed and is divided equally between both.
D) The second person must pay compensation to the first marker.

Key Takeaway
Tahjir establishes a priority right, not ownership; the three-year waiting period is a religious guideline, and actual revival determines ownership.

Liability for Second Well Dug Outside First Well's Harim
Ruling on liability for second well causing water loss when dug outside harim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for a second well dug outside the harim and explain why the second digger is not liable.

Core Idea
No liability without transgression: digging beyond the harim is not ta'addi.

In this lesson, we examine a case from Al-Hidayah where a second well, dug beyond the harim of an existing one, causes the first well to lose water. The ruling turns on the concept of harim and transgression. Understanding this clarifies when harm to property triggers liability and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Define the harim
Recall that the harim of a well is a protected area of 40 cubits around it; no one else may dig a well within this zone.
This distance is specific to wells in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the second well
Confirm that the second well was dug beyond the 40-cubit harim of the first. This is the key factual condition.
3
Determine transgression
Since the second well is outside the harim, the digger is not muta'addi (transgressing). Hanafi law requires ta'addi for liability.
Transgression means exceeding one's right; digging on one's own land within one's right is not transgression.
4
Apply the liability rule
Conclude: no liability (la shay'a 'alayh) for the water loss, even though harm occurred, because the act was lawful.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Consider harim rights of the second well
The second well also needs a harim. It receives harim on three sides, but not on the side of the first well, because the first owner's right is precedent.
This prevents a conflict of rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان حفر الثانى بيرا وراء حريم الأولى فذهب ماء البير الاولى لاشيء عليه لانه غير متعد في حفرها وللثاني الحريم من الجوانب الثلاثة دون الجانب الاول لسبق ملك الحافر الاول فيه ترجمہ اور اگر دوسرے نے کنواں کھودا پہلے کے حریم سے باہر پس پہلے کنویں کا پانی ختم ہو گیا تو اس پر (ثانی پر ) کوئی ضمان نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے کھودنے میں متعدی نہیں ہے اور دوسرے کو تین طرف سے حریم ملے گا نہ کہ پہلے کی جانب میں حافر اول کی ملکیت کے مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے اس میں۔ تشریح دوسرے نے پہلے کنویں کے حریم سے باہر یعنی چالیس ذراع ہٹ کر کنواں کھودا جس کی وجہ سے پہلے کنویں کا پانی ختم ہو گیا تو دوسرے پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کی جانب سے کوئی تعدی نہیں پائی گئی کیونکہ اس نے اول کے حریم سے باہر کنواں کھودا ہے پھر دوسرے کنویں کو بھی حریم چاہیے تو فرمایا کہ پہلے کنویں کی جانب میں تو پہلے کنویں کا حریم ہے چالیس ذراع تک اس میں تو دوسرے کو حریم نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ اس سمت پہلے کی ملک مقدم ہے البتہ اس جانب کے علاوہ باقی تینوں جانبوں میں دوسرے کو حریم ملے گا۔ تنبیہ پانی زمین کے نیچے کسی کی ملکیت نہیں ہے تو اس پر یہ جبر نہیں ہو سکتا کہ یہاں سے اپنا کنواں بنانے جبکہ اس نے کوئی تعدی نہیں کی اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی کی دکان ہے۔ اور اس چیز کی دکان دوسرے نے اس کے برابر میں کرلی جس سے پہلی دکان ٹھپ ہوگئی تو دوسرے پر کوئی ضمان نہیں ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۳۵ ج ۲
And if a second person digs a well beyond the harim of the first, and the water of the first well disappears, nothing is incumbent upon him because he is not transgressing in digging it. And the second well gets harim on three sides except the side of the first because the ownership of the first digger is precedent in that side. Translation: And if the second person dug a well outside the harim of the first, then the water of the first well disappeared, there is no liability on him (the second) because he was not transgressing in digging it. And the second will get harim on three sides and not on the side of the first because the ownership of the first digger is precedent in that side. Explanation: The second person dug a well outside the harim of the first, i.e., forty cubits away, causing the first well's water to disappear. There will be no liability on the second because there was no transgression from his side since he dug outside the first's harim. Then the second well also needs a harim. So it is stated that on the side of the first well, the first well's harim is forty cubits, so the second will not get harim there because the ownership of the first is precedent in that direction. However, on the other three sides, the second will get harim. Note: Water underground is not owned by anyone, so he cannot be prevented from digging his own well as long as he did not transgress. And this is like someone's shop; another person opens a shop next to it causing the first to close, there is no liability. Majma' al-Anhur vol. 2 p. 535.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the digging of wells in dead land. The key principle is that there is no liability for damage caused to another's well if the actor was not legally transgressing. The second well is considered permissible if dug beyond the harim of the first, which is forty cubits. Consequently, the second well only gets its own harim on three sides, as the first's ownership precedes on one side. The note clarifies that underground water is not private property; thus, no one can force another not to dig a well if it is not within the prohibited harim. The analogy of two shops illustrates the concept of indirect harm without liability.

Key Terms
حریم (harim): A protected area around a well, tree, or structure that no one else may use for a similar purpose; for a well it is 40 cubits.
متعدی (muta'addi): One who transgresses legally by doing an action that harms another without right, such as digging within the harim of another's well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person digs a well 50 cubits away from an existing well. The first well's water disappears. Is the second digger liable according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes, because he caused harm.
B) No, because he dug outside the harim (40 cubits).
C) Yes, because water is communal property.
D) No, because all wells are permitted anywhere.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, liability for damage requires transgression (ta'addi); digging outside the harim does not incur liability even if it causes the neighboring well to dry up.

6 min
Prohibition of Digging a Canal or Installing a Water-Mill from a Shared Canal
Ruling with condition and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on digging a canal or installing a water-mill from a shared canal, identify the conditions for prohibition, and apply the exception when no harm is caused and the structure is on the owner's own land.

Core Idea
A partner in a shared canal cannot unilaterally alter it unless no harm is caused and the action is on his own land.

The Hanafi school strictly protects the rights of partners in shared property. The following passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario: one partner wishing to dig a new branch canal or install a water-mill on a shared canal. The ruling establishes that any such alteration requires the consent of all partners, unless two conditions are met: the alteration causes no harm to the canal or water flow, and it is carried out on the partner's own land. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general ruling
The passage states the act: digging a canal or installing a water-mill from a shared canal. The general ruling is: absolutely prohibited without the consent of all partners.
This is the default position; consent must be explicit or implied.
2
Understand the rationale
The prohibition is due to two harms: breaking the canal bank (khasm al-daffah) and occupying shared space with a structure (shughl mawdi' mushtarak bi al-bina'). These are considered darar (harm) to the partners' collective rights.
The 'illa is the harm caused to the partners.
3
Recognize the exception
The exception applies when (1) the water-mill does not harm the canal or its water flow, and (2) it is placed on the partner's own land, not on the shared bank. In that case, it is permissible because it is a disposal of one's own property without harm.
The exception only applies if both conditions are fulfilled.
4
Apply to analogous devices
The commentary extends the same ruling to waterwheel and pulley (daliyah and saniyah), indicating that any structure using the shared canal's water is subject to the same rule.
The 'illa is the same: potential harm to the canal and water.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
While the Hanafi school is strict, other madhhabs may allow more permissive use of shared canals. The Hanafi position is based on the principle of la darar wa la dirar and the necessity of unanimous consent.
This ikhtilaf is recognized as valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخصوص مشترک نہر سے کوئی دوسری نہر کھودنا چاہے تو اپنے ساتھیوں کی اجازت کے بغیر نہیں کھود سکتا
وليس لاحدهم ان يكرى منه نهرا او ينصب عليه رحى ماء الا برضى اصحابه لان فيه كسر ضفة النهر وشغل موضع مشترك بالبناء الا ان يكون رحى لا يضر بالنهر ولا بالماء ويكون موضعها في ارض صاحبها لانه تصرف في ملك نفسه ولا ضرر في حق غيره
ترجمہ اور ان میں سے کسی کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ اس سے نہر کھودے یا نہر پر پن چکی لگائے مگر اپنے ساتھیوں کی رضامندی سے اس لئے کہ اس میں نہر کے کنارے کو توڑنا ہے اور مشترک جگہ کو عمارت میں مشغول کرنا ہے مگر یہ کہ پن چکی نہر اور پانی کو نقصان نہ پہنچائے اور اس کی جگہ اس کے مالک کی زمین میں ہو اس لئے کہ یہ اپنی ملکیت میں تصرف ہے اور اس کے غیر کے حق میں کوئی ضرر نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مخصوص مشترک نہر میں سے کوئی دوسری نہر کھودنا چاہتا ہے تو اپنے ساتھیوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر نہیں کر سکتا ، اسی طرح نہر مخصوص مشترک کے کنارے پر پن چکی لگانا چاہتا ہے تو اپنے ساتھیوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر نہیں لگا سکتا، کیونکہ اس میں نہر کا کنارا توڑنا پڑے گا نیز پن چکی میں مشترک جگہ کو اپنی عمارت نہیں گھیر لے گا اور یہ دونوں ممنوع ہیں اور اگر پن چکی ایسی ہو کہ اس سے نہر کو اور اس کے پانی کوکوئی نقصان نہیں پہنچتا اور اپنی جگہ میں پن چکی لگاتا ہے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ اپنی ملک میں تصرف ہے جس میں کسی کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے۔
تنبیہ پن چکی ، یعنی پانی سے چلنے والی آٹا پینے والی چکی جو پہلے نہر کے کناروں پر لگائی جاتی تھی جہاں جھال وغیرہ ہوتا کہ پانی زور سے پڑے اور پانی کے پریشر سے چکی چلے اب تو چکی بجلی سے اور انجن سے چلائی جاتی ہیں اور وہ پہلا رواج ختم ہو گیا۔
نہر کے نقصان کا مصداق
ومعنى الضرر بالنهر ما بيناه من كسر ضفته وبالماء ان يتغير عن سننه الذى كان يجرى عليه والدالية والسانية نظير الرحى
ترجمہ اور نہر کے نقصان کے وہی معنی ہیں جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں یعنی نہر کا کنارہ توڑنا اور پانی کا ضرر یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنی اس روش سے متغیر ہو جائے جس پر وہ جاری تھا اور رہٹ اور چرس پن چکی کے درجہ میں ہے۔
تشریح جو ماقبل میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اگر نہر اور پانی کا نقصان نہ ہو تو جائز ہے تو نہر کے نقصان سے یہ مراد ہے کہ اس کا کنارا توڑ دیا جائے۔ اور پانی کے نقصان سے یہ مراد ہے کہ وہ پہلے طریقہ پر نہ ہے اور پن چکی لگانے کا جو حکم ہے وہی حکم رہٹ اور چرس لگانے کا ہے کہ
اگر مضر ہو تو جائز نہیں مگر باجازت۔ اور اگر مضر نہ ہو اور اپنی جگہ میں ہو تو جائز ہے۔
If someone wants to dig another canal from a shared canal, he cannot do so without the consent of his partners. And none of them has the right to dig a canal from it or install a water-mill on it except with the consent of his partners, because in that there is breaking the bank of the canal and occupying the shared place with a structure. Unless the water-mill does not harm the canal or the water, and its place is in his own land, because it is a disposal in his own property and there is no harm to anyone else. Translation: And none of them has the right to dig a canal from it or install a water-mill on it except with the consent of his partners, because in that there is breaking the bank of the canal and occupying the shared place with a structure. Unless the water-mill does not harm the canal or the water, and its place is in his own land, because it is a disposal in his own property and there is no harm to anyone else. Commentary: One partner wants to dig another canal from the shared canal; he cannot do so without the consent of his partners. Similarly, if he wants to install a water-mill on the bank of the shared canal, he cannot do so without the consent of his partners, because it would require breaking the bank and also the water-mill would occupy the shared space. Both are prohibited. But if the water-mill does not harm the canal or its water, and he installs it on his own land, then it is permissible because it is a disposal in his own property with no harm to anyone. Note: A water-mill is a mill that runs on water, previously installed on canal banks where there was a waterfall; now mills run on electricity and engines. Meaning of harm to the canal: And the meaning of harm to the canal is what we explained: breaking its bank. And harm to the water is that it changes from its course on which it used to flow. The waterwheel and the pulley are analogous to the water-mill. Translation: And the meaning of harm to the canal is what we have explained: breaking its bank. And harm to the water is that it changes from its original course. The waterwheel and the pulley are similar to the water-mill. Commentary: It was said before that if there is no harm to the canal or water, then it is permissible. Harm to the canal means its bank is broken, and harm to the water means it does not flow in its previous way. The same ruling as for the water-mill applies to the waterwheel and pulley: if they cause harm, they are impermissible without permission; if no harm and on own land, permissible.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with its conditions and exceptions. The passage establishes that no partner in a shared canal has the right to dig another branch canal or install a water-mill without the consent of all partners. The reason ('illa) is that such actions involve breaking the canal bank and occupying the shared space with a structure, both of which harm the collective rights. However, an exception is made: if the water-mill does not harm the canal or its water flow, and the mill is placed on the partner's own private land (not on the shared canal bank), then it is permissible because it is a disposal of one's own property without causing harm to others. The commentary explains that the same ruling applies to other water devices like the waterwheel (daliyah) and pulley (saniyah). The note clarifies the historical context of water-mills.

Key Terms
نهر مشترك (nahr mushtarak): A canal jointly owned by multiple partners with shared rights to its use.
رحى ماء (raha ma'): A water-powered mill installed on a canal.
ضرر (darar): Harm or damage, specifically breaking the canal bank or diverting water flow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible for a partner to install a water-mill on a shared canal without consent?
A) When the mill is small and portable.
B) When it causes no harm to the canal or water and is placed on the partner's own land.
C) When the mill is for grinding grain for the community.
D) When the mill is temporary and used only during high water.

Key Takeaway
A partner in a shared canal may not unilaterally dig or install structures without consent, unless the action causes no harm and is on his own land.

Prohibition of Building a Bridge over a Shared Canal
Ruling on bridge construction as property disposal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building a bridge over a shared canal and apply the analogy (qiyas) to shared property disputes.

Core Idea
No partner may build on shared property without unanimous consent; a bridge over a shared canal is like a private path.

A bridge over a shared canal may seem harmless, but the Hanafi school prohibits it without the consent of all partners. This ruling is based on an analogy to a private path shared among a group—no one can unilaterally alter it. In this lesson, we unpack the legal reasoning and the key condition of unanimous agreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Building a bridge or vault over a shared canal.) What is the default hukm (haram without consent, mubah with consent)?
2
Locate the Analogy (Asl)
The text compares the shared canal to a private path (tariq khas) used by a group. What is the ruling on that asl? No individual may dispose of or build on it without the consent of all.
3
Identify the Effective Cause (Illa)
What is the common attribute linking the asl and the far'? Shared property where each partner has equal rights to use and dispose. The illa is joint ownership without permission to act unilaterally.
4
Apply the Qiyas to the New Case (Far')
Since the canal is shared property like the path, the same ruling applies: building a bridge requires unanimous consent. If consent is absent, the act is prohibited.
5
Note the Exception: Consent Makes It Permissible
The text states that if all partners agree, it becomes permissible. This is not an annulment of the prohibition but a removal of the preventing factor (lack of consent).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخصوص نہر پر پل بنانے کا حکم
ولا يتخذ عليه جسرا ولا قنطرة بمنزلة طريق خاص بين قوم
ترجمہ اور نہ بنائے اس پر پل کسی قوم کے درمیان طریق خاص کے درجہ میں۔
تشریح اسی طرح کسی شریک کو حق نہیں ہے کہ نہر مخصوص مشترک پر لکڑی وغیرہ کا یا پختہ پل بنائے جیسے وہ راستہ جو چند آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو ان میں سے کسی کو یہ حق نہیں کہ راستہ میں تصرف کرے ایسے ہی یہاں البتہ اگر شرکاء راضی ہوں تو جائز ہے۔
Ruling on building a bridge over a shared canal: And he should not make a bridge or a vault over it, as it is like a private path between a people. Translation: And do not build a bridge over it, of the status of a private path among a people. Commentary: Similarly, no partner has the right to build a wooden or permanent bridge over the shared canal, just like a path shared among several people; none of them has the right to dispose of the path. Here too, if the partners agree, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a ruling statement comparing a shared canal to a shared path. The text prohibits any partner from building a bridge over a shared canal without the consent of all partners. The analogy (qiyas) is that a shared canal is like a private road used by a group of people: no individual can unilaterally build structures on it. However, if all partners agree, it becomes permissible. The commentary emphasizes that this applies to any type of bridge, whether wood or permanent.

Key Terms
جسر (jisr): A bridge built over a canal for passage
قنطرة (qantarah): A vaulted arch or aqueduct; also considered a structure on shared space
طريق خاص (tariq khas): A private path used by a specific group of people

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is building a bridge over a shared canal prohibited without consent?
A) Because it blocks the water flow.
B) Because it is analogous to a shared path where no one can dispose without consent.
C) Because bridges are expensive and unfair.
D) Because it requires government permission.

Key Takeaway
Building any structure on shared property, even a bridge, requires unanimous consent of all partners; the prohibition stems from the principle of partnership, not harm.

Permissibility of Building a Bridge on a Private Canal Derived from a Shared Canal
Exception when one owns a private canal from the shared one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building structures on a private canal derived from a shared source and identify the condition that must be satisfied.

Core Idea
Disposal in one's exclusive property is permitted as long as it does not harm others.

In Hanafi fiqh, water rights and property ownership are carefully balanced. When a person, with the consent of the shared canal owners, digs a private branch, that branch becomes his exclusive property. This lesson examines the ruling on building or demolishing a bridge on such a private canal, focusing on the key condition: no increase in water intake that harms the original partners.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Building or demolishing a bridge on a private canal derived from a shared source. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah).
2
Locate the talil (reason)
The text states: 'because he disposes in his exclusive property' (يتصرف فى خالص ملكه). This principle of ownership is the foundation.
The Arabic phrase 'كhalis milkihi' is key.
3
Note the condition
The act must not increase the owner's water intake from the shared source. The text explicitly says: 'ولا يزيد ذلك فى اخذ الماء' (and that does not increase the water intake).
This ensures no harm to the other partners.
4
Distinguish from shared property
If the canal were still shared (not made private with permission), the ruling would be different – any structure would require the consent of all partners. The distinction hinges on exclusive ownership.
The phrase 'خلاف' indicates the contrast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرکاء کی اجازت سے مشترکہ نہر سے ایک نہر نکالی اب اپنی نہر پر پل بنانا چاہے تو حق حاصل ہے بخلاف ما اذا كان لواحد نهر خاص يأخذ من نهر خاص بين قوم فاراد ان يقنطر عليه ويستوثق منه له ذلك اوكان مقنطرا مستوثقا فاراد ان ينقض ذلك ولا يزيد ذلك فى اخذ الماء حيث يكون له ذلك لانه يتصرف فى خالص ملكه وضعا ورفعا ولا ضرر بالشركاء باخذ زيادة الماء
ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ کسی کی خاص نہر ہو جو کسی قوم کے درمیان خاص نہر سے لی ہے پس اس نے ارادہ کیا کہ اس پر پل بنا اور اس کو مضبوط کرے تو اس کو اس کا حق ہے یا وہ مضبوط پل تھا تو اس نے اس کو توڑنے کا ارادہ کیا اور یہ پانی لینے میں اضافہ نہیں کرتا تو اس کو اس کا حق ہوا اسلئے کہ وہ خاص اپنی ملکیت میں تصرف کرتا ہے باعتبار بنانے اور اکھاڑنے کے اور شرکاء کا کوئی ضرر نہیں پانی کی زیاتی کو لینے میں۔
تشریح زید نے ایک مشترک خاص نہر سے ان کی اجازت سے ایک نہر نکالی اب وہ اپنی شہر پر پل بنانا چاہتا ہے تو چونکہ اس میں کسی کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے تو یہ جائز ہے پا پہلے سے اس پر پل تھا اس کو ہٹانا چاہتا ہے تو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ اس میں کسی کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے وہ اپنی ملک میں تصرف کر رہا ہے جبکہ ایسا کرنے میں پانی کی آمد میں کوئی اضافہ نہیں ہوتا لہذا وضع بنانا (نفع اٹھانا) میں اس کو اختیار ہے۔
If from a shared canal with permission one canal is taken, now if he wants to build a bridge on his own canal, he has the right. Contrary to when someone has a private canal that takes water from a private canal among a people, and he wants to build a bridge on it and strengthen it, he has that right. Or if it was a strengthened bridge and he wants to demolish it, and that does not increase the water intake, he has that right, because he disposes in his exclusive property by building and removing, and there is no harm to the partners by taking extra water. Translation: Contrary to the case when someone has a private canal that takes water from a private canal among a people, so he intends to build a bridge on it and strengthen it, he has that right. Or if it was a strengthened bridge and he intends to demolish it, and this does not increase the water intake, he has that right because he disposes in his exclusive property by building and demolishing, and there is no harm to the partners in taking extra water. Commentary: Zayd took a canal from a shared special canal with their permission; now he wants to build a bridge on his own canal, since there is no harm, it is permissible. If there was already a bridge and he wants to remove it, also permissible, because he disposes in his own property without increasing water flow.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that distinguishes the case of a private canal derived from a shared canal with permission. The text establishes that if a person has constructed a private canal from a shared canal with the partners' consent, then he has full rights over that private canal. He may build a bridge on it, strengthen it, or demolish an existing bridge, as long as these actions do not increase his water intake from the shared source. The reason ('illa) is that he is disposing of his own exclusive property, and no harm comes to the other partners. The commentary reinforces this by giving the example of Zayd.

Key Terms
نهر خاص (nahr khas): A private canal that is owned by an individual and takes water from a shared source with permission.
تصرف في خالص ملكه (tasarruf fi khalis milkihi): Disposal in one's pure ownership – a key justification for permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is necessary for a partner to build a bridge on a canal he dug from a shared canal?
A) All partners must agree to the bridge.
B) The bridge must not increase water intake from the shared source.
C) The bridge must be made of wood.
D) The bridge must be removable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a person may build a bridge on his private canal derived with permission from a shared source, provided it does not increase his water intake and harm the partners.

Prohibition of Widening the Mouth of a Shared Canal
Ruling on widening a canal mouth as harmful

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that widening the mouth of a shared canal is haram and explain the two-part legal cause (breaking the bank and exceeding one's share).

Core Idea
Widening your canal mouth steals water and breaks the bank – it's haram.

This passage addresses a specific muamalat case: a partner in a shared water source wants to widen his canal's intake. The Hanafi ruling is a clear prohibition based on two interconnected harms: physical damage to the bank and unjust appropriation of water beyond one's share. Let's walk through the reasoning and see how this ruling safeguards communal rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is widening the mouth (fam al-nahr) of a canal that draws from a shared source. The ruling is that the partner is to be prevented from doing so – i.e., it is prohibited (haram).
2
Locate the legal cause (illah)
The text gives the reason: 'because it breaks the bank of the canal and increases beyond his right in taking water.' This two-part illah is the basis of the prohibition.
Both parts must be present in the illah; either alone would suffice for prohibition.
3
Analyze the two components of the illah
First, breaking the bank (kasr al-diffa) causes direct harm to the shared property. Second, increasing water intake beyond one's share (ziyada 'ala qadr haqqihi) is an injustice (zulm) against the other partners.
The combination of harm (darar) and injustice (dhulm) makes the act clearly haram.
4
Identify the legal characterization of the actor
The commentary labels the person as 'ghasib' (usurper) – one who wrongfully takes others' rights. This reinforces that the act is not merely disliked but a transgression.
The term ghasib carries serious legal consequences in Hanafi fiqh (e.g., liability for damages).
5
Apply the ruling to similar situations
Any action that similarly increases one's share of a common resource at the expense of others – e.g., extending a fence into shared land, diverting more water from a common stream – would fall under the same prohibition.
The principle is prevention of harm (la darar wa la dirar) and protection of proportional rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہر کا منہ کشادہ کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے
ويمنع من أن يوسع فم النهر لانه يكسر ضفة النهر ويزيد على مقدار حقه في اخذ الماء
ترجمہ اور اس کو منع کیا جائے گا نہر کا منہ کشادہ کرنے سے اس لئے کہ وہ توڑے گا نہر کا کنارا اور اضافہ کرے گا اپنے حق کی مقدار پر پانی لینے میں۔
تشریح یعنی مذکورہ اشیاء سے تو اس کو روکا نہیں گیا تھا لیکن اگر وہ اپنی نہر کا منہ چوڑا کرنا چاہے تو اس سے اس کو منع کیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ غاصب ہے دوسروں کے حقوق ضائع کرنے والا ہے۔
Permission to widen the mouth of the canal is not given. And he will be prevented from widening the mouth of the canal, because it breaks the bank of the canal and increases beyond his right in taking water. Translation: He will be prevented from widening the mouth of the canal, because he will break the bank and increase beyond the measure of his right in taking water. Commentary: He was not prevented from the previous things, but if he wants to widen the mouth of his canal, he will be prevented from that, because he is an usurper and destroyer of others' rights.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a ruling statement prohibiting a partner from widening the mouth of his canal that draws water from a shared source. The reason is twofold: first, it involves breaking the canal bank (a harmful act), and second, it increases the amount of water he can draw beyond his rightful share. The commentary emphasizes that while he was not prevented from other actions (like building a bridge on his private canal), widening the mouth is strictly forbidden because it unjustly increases his water intake at the expense of other partners. Such an act is described as 'غاصب' (usurper).

Key Terms
فم النهر (fam al-nahr): The mouth or inlet of a canal where it takes water from the main source.
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; one who wrongfully appropriates the rights of others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a partner prevented from widening the mouth of his canal from a shared source?
A) Because it requires heavy labor.
B) Because it breaks the canal bank and increases his water intake beyond his share.
C) Because the canal might dry up.
D) Because it looks ugly.

Key Takeaway
Widening a canal mouth from a shared source is haram because it breaks the bank and unjustly increases one's water share, making the doer a usurper.

Taking Water from a Shared Canal to Another Land
Ruling on taking water from a shared canal to another land without right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a partner takes water from a shared canal to a land without water rights, and identify the exception that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
A partner cannot use his share of canal water for a different land unless all partners consent or he stores water after filling his own land and blocks the canal mouth.

This lesson examines a common scenario in agricultural partnerships: water rights in shared canals. The Hanafi school strictly prohibits a partner from using the water for a land that has no share in that canal, even indirectly. However, there is one exception when the water is stored after properly filling the entitled land and blocking the canal mouth, and another when all partners give unanimous permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Focus on the act of a partner taking water from a shared canal to a land that does not have a right (sharb) in that canal. Determine the legal ruling (haram, permissible with conditions).
The key is the absence of sharb for the target land.
2
State the general ruling and its basis
The text states it is not permissible (jā'iz nahī). This is because taking water for a land without right exceeds one's share and leads to potential disputes.
The basis is protecting each partner's precise share.
3
Identify the two prohibited methods
The passage describes two prohibited scenarios: (1) directly diverting water to the other land, (2) letting water flow through the first land to reach the second (the first absorbs some, so it's still exceeding the share).
Even indirect use is prohibited because the first land absorbs water.
4
Recognize the exceptions
Two exceptions: (a) if all partners unanimously give permission, it becomes permissible; (b) if the partner fills his entitled land, blocks the canal mouth (dahanah), and then uses the stored water for the other land, it is permissible because he no longer draws from the canal.
Blocking the mouth is crucial; without it, the act remains prohibited.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Test your understanding by considering a case where a partner has two lands, one with right. Determine whether the action is permissible or prohibited, and state the applicable exception if any.
Always check if the canal mouth has been blocked or if all partners consented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح اگر شرکاء میں سے کوئی شریک نہر کا پانی اپنی دوسری زمین میں لے جائے جس کا شرب اس نہر میں نہیں ہے تو اس کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں ورنہ کچھ زمانہ گذرنے کے بعد وہ کہے گا کہ یہ تو میرا حق ہے لہذا اس کو پہلے ہی روک دیا جائیگا۔ تنبیہ لیکن اگر شرکاء راضی ہو جائیں اور اجازت دیں تو جائز ہے۔
اگر پہلی زمین بھر جائے اسی سے دوسری زمین کو لگانا چاہے تو بھی جائز نہیں وكذا اذا اراد ان يسوق شربه فى ارضه الاولى حتى ينتهى الى هذه الأرض الأخرى لانه يستوفي زيادة على حقه اذ الأرض الأولى تنشف بعض الماء قبل ان يسقى الاخرى ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ ارادہ اس نے کیا کہ اپنے شرب کو اپنی پہلی زمین میں لے جائے یہاں تک وہ پہنچ جائے اس دوسری زمین تک اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے حق سے زیادہ وصول کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ پہلی زمین کچھ پانی جذب کرے گی اس سے پہلے کہ وہ دوسری کو سیراب کرے۔ تشریح کسی کی دو زمینیں ہیں ان میں سے ایک کا شرب اس نہر پر ہے اور دوسری کا نہیں تو دوسری میں پانی لے جانا جائز نہیں ہے لیکن اگر اس نے پہلی زمین کو اتنا بھر دیا کہ پھر اس سے دوسری زمین کو بھر سکے یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کا حق ایک زمین کو بھرنے کا تھا اور اس نے دو زمینوں کو بھر لیا ہے کیونکہ پہلی زمین اپنے اندر پانی جذب کرے گی اس کے بعد دوسری کی جانب آئے گا خلاصہ کلام اول اور یہ دونوں صورتیں جائز نہیں ہیں۔ تنبیہ لیکن اگر اس نے پہلی زمین بھر کر نہر کا دہانہ بند کر دیا اور پھر اس نے اس پانی سے دوسری زمین کو سیراب کیا تو جائز ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے اس وقت اپنے حق سے زیادہ نہیں لیا اور اگر دہانہ بند نہ کیا ہو تو جائز نہیں ہے۔
Explanation: If one of the partners takes the water of the canal to his other land which does not have a right of irrigation in that canal, then this is not permissible for him, otherwise after some time he will say: This is my right, therefore he should be stopped from the beginning. Note: But if the partners agree and give permission, then it is permissible. If the first land is filled and he wants to irrigate the second land from it, then also it is not permissible. And similarly if he intends to convey his water to his first land until it reaches this other land, because he takes more than his right, as the first land absorbs some water before it irrigates the other. Explanation: Someone has two lands, one of which has a right of irrigation in this canal and the other does not, so taking water to the second is not permissible. But if he filled the first land so much that from it he can fill the second, this also is not permissible, because his right was to fill one land and he has filled two lands, because the first land absorbs water inside it before it goes to the other. Summary: The first and these two forms are not permissible. Note: But if he filled the first land and blocked the mouth of the canal, and then irrigated the second land with that water, then it is permissible, because he did not take more than his right at that time; and if he did not block the mouth, then it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) regarding water rights in a shared canal. The commentator explains that a partner cannot use the shared water for a different land that has no right to that canal, even indirectly. The key principle: the right is limited to the specific land attached to the canal. Three cases are discussed: (1) directly taking water to another land is unlawful; (2) letting water pass through the first land to reach the second is also unlawful because the first absorbs some, resulting in excessive use; (3) if the partner fills his first land, then blocks the canal mouth, and uses that stored water for the second, it becomes permissible because he no longer draws from the shared source. The prohibition is based on preventing harm to other partners' rights. All examples are Hanafi, consistent with the madhhab's strict protection of water shares.

Key Terms
شرب (sharb): Right of irrigation or water share attached to a specific land.
نہر مشترک (nahr mushtarak): A canal shared among partners where each has a defined share of water.
دہانہ (dahanah): The mouth or opening of a canal where water enters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a partner fills his first land and then uses that stored water to irrigate his second land that has no right in the canal?
A) It is permissible unconditionally.
B) It is prohibited because he exceeds his right.
C) It is permissible only if he blocks the canal mouth before storing.
D) It is makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
In a shared canal, a partner's water right is strictly attached to his specific land; transferring it to another land is prohibited unless all partners consent or he stores the water after properly filling his entitled land and blocking the canal mouth.

Analogy of Shared Canal with Shared Pathway
Analogical proof comparing canal rights to pathway rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi qiyas jaliy to compare shared property cases and state the ruling on increasing burden without consent.

Core Idea
Increasing burden on shared property without consent is prohibited, whether canal or pathway.

This passage uses qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) to strengthen a ruling on shared canal by comparing it to a shared pathway. The commentator identifies the effective cause ('illa) as increasing the burden on the shared property without consent. Understanding this analogy helps you derive rulings in new cases of co-ownership rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl)
The asl is a partner taking water from a shared canal to land that has no right to that water.
This is the established case with a known ruling.
2
State the ruling in the asl
The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram) because it harms other partners by exceeding their share.
The ruling is based on preventing harm.
3
Identify the new case (far')
The far' is a partner opening a new door from a shared pathway to another house that has a different occupant.
The new case is analogous to the asl.
4
Extract the effective cause ('illa)
The 'illa is increasing the burden on the shared property without the consent of the other partners.
This 'illa is clear and directly observable (jaliy).
5
Transfer the ruling
Since the 'illa is present in the far', the same ruling of prohibition applies: opening the new door is haram without consent.
An exception exists if the new door does not bring an additional occupant (no increase in burden).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسئلہ مذکورہ کی نظیر وهو نظير طريق مشترك اذا اراد احدهم ان يفتح فيه بابا الى دار اخرى ساكنها غير ساكن هذه الدار التي فتح هذا الباب ترجمہ اور یہ مشترک راستہ کی نظیر ہے جبکہ ارادہ کرے ان میں سے ایک کہ کھولدے اس میں دروازہ دوسرے گھر کی جانب جس کا رہنے والا اس گھر کے رہنے والے کے علاوہ ہے جس کا دروازہ اس راستہ کی جانب ہے۔ تشریح ایک مشترک راستہ ہے جس میں مثلاً دو آدمی شریک ہیں ان میں سے ایک زید ہے جس کے دو گھر ہیں ایک کا دروازہ اسی راستہ پر ہے اور دوسرے مکان کا دروازہ اس راستہ میں نہیں ہے اور اس میں زید نے کسی اور کو آباد کر رکھا ہے اب زید چاہتا ہے کہ اس کا راستہ بھی یہی راستہ ہو جائے اور اس کا دروازہ اسی راستہ پر کھول دیا جائے تو زید کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مشترک راستہ میں گذرنے والوں کی تعداد بڑھ جائے گی البتہ اگر اس میں رہنے والا کوئی اور نہ ہو تو زید کو دروازہ کھولنے کا حق ہے کیونکہ اس میں گذرنے والوں کی تعداد میں کچھ اضافہ نہ ہوگا۔ اسی طرح مذکورہ دوسری زمین کا اس نہر میں جب شرب نہیں ہے تو زید کو حق نہیں ہے کہ اس کا پانی وہاں لیجائے تا کہ اراضی میں اضافہ نہ ہو اور وہ زمین اس میں داخل نہ ہو سکے جس کا اس میں حق نہیں ہے۔
Analogy of the mentioned issue: And it is analogous to a shared pathway, when one of them intends to open a door in it to another house whose inhabitant is other than the inhabitant of this house for which the door was opened. Translation: And this is analogous to a shared pathway, when one of them intends to open a door in it to another house whose inhabitant is other than the inhabitant of the house that has a door on that pathway. Explanation: There is a shared pathway, for example, two people are partners, one of them is Zaid who has two houses, one has a door on this pathway and the other house's door is not on this pathway, and Zaid has settled someone else in it. Now Zaid wants that this pathway also becomes his way and his door be opened on this pathway, then Zaid will not have this right, because the number of passersby on the shared pathway would increase. However, if there is no other occupant, then Zaid has the right to open a door, because the number of passersby would not increase. Similarly, in the mentioned second land, since it has no right of irrigation in this canal, Zaid has no right to take the water there, so that the lands may not increase and that land which has no right may not enter into it.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to strengthen the previous ruling. The commentator draws a parallel between a shared canal and a shared pathway. In both, a partner cannot increase the burden on the shared property without the consent of the other partners. The 'illa (effective cause) is the increase in usage burden: in the pathway, opening a new door increases traffic; in the canal, irrigating additional land increases water consumption. This is a strong analogy (qiyas jaliy) because the 'illa is obvious and the ruling is directly transferred. The Hanafi school consistently applies this principle to shared rights.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
طریق مشترک (tariq mushtarak): A pathway shared among owners, each having right of passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the analogy of the shared pathway, when is it permissible for a partner to open a new door onto the pathway?
A) Whenever he wants, as he is a partner.
B) Only if the other partner agrees.
C) Only if the new door does not increase the number of occupants using the pathway.
D) Never, because it always increases burden.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas jaliy demonstrates that increasing burden on shared property without consent is prohibited, whether in a canal or a pathway.

Blocking Holes and Changing Water Distribution Method
Two rulings on water distribution modification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on unilateral modification of shared water distribution and explain why mutual changes are treated as a revocable loan (i'arah).

Core Idea
You cannot block water holes or change distribution method without mutual consent; any change is always revocable.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two distinct but related scenarios in shared canal water rights. First, a partner wishes to block some holes to prevent waterlogging on his own land. Second, a partner proposes to replace the existing hole-based distribution with a time-based rotation. The Hanafi school prohibits both unilateral actions, emphasizing that established rights of all partners are inviolable. If partners mutually agree to a change, it is treated as a revocable loan (i'arah), not a binding sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proposed modifications
The passage presents two cases: (1) blocking some of the existing holes to reduce water flow to one's own land, and (2) switching from hole-based distribution to alternating days. Recognize that both involve changing an established water distribution system without the other partner's consent.
The private canal has fixed holes (kuwwa) that define each partner's share.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For blocking holes: the upper partner does not have the right to block any holes, even if his land is harmed, because it harms the other partner. For changing to days: it is not permissible unless both agree; if they do agree, it is considered a loan (i'arah) and can be revoked by either party or their heirs.
The text analogizes blocking holes to widening them – both are unauthorized dispositions of common property.
3
Analyze the legal basis: harm and i'arah classification
The prohibition is based on preventing harm (darar) to the partner with an established right. When a mutually agreed change occurs, it cannot be a sale or exchange of water shares (which is invalid), so it is classified as a revocable loan (i'arah). This preserves the original rights and allows reversion.
The lender (mu'ir) can revoke at any time; after death, heirs inherit this right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اوپر کی زمین میں رہنے والا شریک بعض سوراخوں کو بند کرنا چاہے تو اسے یہ حق حاصل نہیں ولو اراد الاعلى من الشريكين فى النهر الخاص وفيه كوى بينهما ان يسد بعضها دفعا لفيض الماء عن ارضه كى لا تنزل ليـه مـن رر بالاخر ترجمہ اور اگر ارادہ کیا شریکوں میں سے اوپر والے نے خاص نہر میں اور اس میں ان کے درمیان موریاں ہیں کہ ان میں سے بعض کو بند کر دے اپنی زمین سے پانی بہنے کو دور کرنے کے لئے تا کہ زمین نمناک نہ ہو جائے تو اس کو اس کا حق نہ ہوگا بوجہ اس کے کہ اس میں دوسرے کا ضرر ہے۔
تشریح مبسوط میں صورت مسئلہ یہ مذکور ہے کہ ایک بڑی نہر میں دو آدمیوں کے لئے پانچ موریاں لگی ہوتی ہیں ان میں سے ایک کی زمین اوپر اور دوسرے کی نیچے ہے اب اوپر والا چاہتا ہے کہ ان موریوں میں سے ایک یا دو کو بند کر دے کیونکہ پانی کی کثرت کی وجہ سے زمین نمناک ہوتی ہے تو اس کو اس کا حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ مکان مشترک میں اپنے ساتھی کی رضامندی کے بغیر تصرف ہے تو یہ ایسے ہی جائز نہیں ہے جیسے موری کو کشادہ کرنے کا حق نہیں ہے۔
سوراخوں کے ذریعے تقسیم کو ایام کی تقسیم میں تبدیل کرنے کا حق نہیں وكذا اذا اراد ان يقسم الشرب مناصفة بينهما لان القسمة بالكوى تقدمت الا ان يتراضيا لان الحق لهما وبعد التراضى لصاحب الاسفل ان ينقض ذلك وكذا الورثة من بعده لانه اعارة الشرب فان مبادلة الشرب بالشرب باطل ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی جبکہ ارادہ کیا ان میں سے ایک نے کہ شرب کو آدھا آدھا بانٹ لیں تو جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ موریوں سے تقسیم مقدم ہو چکا ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ دونوں راضی ہو جائیں اس لئے کہ حق ان دونوں کا ہے اور راضی ہونے کے بعد اسفل والے کو حق ہے کہ اس کو توڑ دے اور ایسے ہی اس کے ورثہ کو حق ہے اس کے بعد اس لئے کہ یہ اعارہ شرب ہے اس لئے کہ شرب کا شرب سے تبادلہ باطل ہے۔
تشریح دو شریک ہیں ان کی ایک نہر ہے جس میں دونوں نے اپنی اپنی موریاں لگا رکھی ہیں اب اوپر والا کہتا ہے کہ باری اس طرح طے کر لیں آٹھ دن پوری نہر تم چلاؤ اور آٹھ دن میں تو صاحب اعلیٰ کو اس کا حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ تقسیم پہلے سے موریوں کے ذریعہ ہو چکا ہے البتہ اگر دوسرا شریک بھی راضی ہو تو جائز ہے۔ مگر شرب کا شرب سے تبادلہ تو باطل ہے تو اس کو اعارہ قرار دیا جائے گا اور اعارہ معیر جب چاہے رجوع کرے لہذا صاحب اسفل کو حق ہوگا کہ جب چاہے اس معاہدہ سے رجوع کرے اور اس کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ورثہ کا بھی یہ حق باقی رہے گا کہ جب چاہیں اس معاہدہ کو توڑ کر حسب سابق تقسیم پر عمل کریں۔
The partner living on the upper land wants to block some holes, then he does not have this right. And if the upper of the two partners in a private canal and there are holes (kawi) between them intends to block some of them to prevent the flow of water from his land so that his land does not become saline, then he does not have this right, because in it there is harm to the other. Explanation: In al-Mabsut, the scenario is mentioned: In a large canal, five holes are made for two men, one's land is above and the other's below. Now the upper wants to block one or two of these holes because due to excess water the land becomes saline, then he does not have this right, because this is a disposition in common property without the consent of his partner, so it is not permissible, just as he does not have the right to widen the holes. He does not have the right to change distribution by holes to distribution by days. And similarly, if one of them intends to divide the water equally between them, then it is not permissible, because the division by holes has preceded, unless they both agree, because the right belongs to both; and after agreement, the lower partner has the right to break it, and likewise the heirs after him, because it is a loan (i'arah) of water share, for exchanging water share for water share is invalid. Explanation: Two partners have one canal in which each has fixed his own holes. Now the upper one says: Let us fix a turn such that for eight days you run the whole canal, and for eight days I run. The owner of the upper does not have this right, because division by holes has already been established. However, if the other partner agrees, it is permissible. But exchanging water share for water share is invalid, so it will be considered a loan (i'arah), and the lender (mu'ir) may revoke whenever he wishes. Hence the lower partner has the right to revoke this agreement whenever he wishes, and after his death, his heirs also retain this right to revoke the agreement and revert to the previous division.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct but related rulings about modifying the water distribution system in a shared canal. First, a partner cannot unilaterally block some of the holes (kawi) that distribute water, even to prevent harm to his own land (e.g., waterlogging), because it harms the other partner's share. This is analogized to not being allowed to widen holes without consent. Second, a partner cannot change the established division method from hole-based to time-based (e.g., alternate days) without the other's consent. If they mutually agree, it is valid but as a loan (i'arah), meaning either party can revoke it at any time. The underlying principle: the water share is a defined right, and any change that affects the other's right requires mutual consent; otherwise it is invalid. Both rulings emphasize the strict Hanafi protection of established water rights.

Key Terms
کوی / موری (kuwwa / mori): A hole or sluice in the canal wall to draw water to one's land.
اعارہ (i'arah): A loan or temporary permission that can be revoked by the lender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two partners agree to change from hole-based distribution to time-based distribution, what is the legal nature of this agreement?
A) A binding contract that cannot be changed.
B) A revocable loan (i'arah) of water shares.
C) A sale of water shares.
D) A partnership (shirkah) agreement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, established water distribution rights are protected; any alteration requires mutual consent, and the agreement is revocable as a loan (i'arah).

Two Methods for Selling Shurb to Repay Debt
Provides two methods for selling shurb with land to repay debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two valid methods for selling shurb to repay a deceased's debt and explain why shurb cannot be sold alone.

Core Idea
Shurb cannot be sold alone; it must be annexed to land and sold combined to realize its value for debt repayment.

This passage addresses a practical problem: the deceased owned only a water right (shurb) but has debts. Since shurb cannot be sold independently (as it is not a corporeal asset), the imam must use one of two legal stratagems to convert it into cash. These stratagems preserve the principle while enabling debt repayment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
The text begins by affirming that shurb cannot be sold alone for debt after the owner's death, just as during his lifetime. This is an established Hanafi ruling.
2
Understand the first method
The imam annexes the shurb to someone else's land that lacks shurb, with the landowner's permission, then sells both together. The landowner receives the value of his land without shurb, and the surplus (the value of shurb) goes to the debt.
This requires the landowner's consent.
3
Understand the second method
If no such land is available, the imam purchases a piece of land without shurb from the deceased's estate, annexes the shurb, and sells both. The sale proceeds first cover the land purchase price; the remainder goes to the debt.
This uses estate funds to buy land.
4
Note the overarching principle
Both methods avoid selling shurb alone, which is batil (void), but allow its value to be realized for debt repayment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يباع الشرب في دين صاحبه بعد موته بدون ارض كما في حال حياته وكيف يصنع الامام الاصح ان يضم الى ارض لا شرب لها فيبيعها باذن صاحبها ثم ينظر الى قسمة الارض مع الشرب وبدونه فيصرف التفاوت الى قضاء الدين وان لم يجد ذلك اشترى على تركة الميت ارضا بغير شرب ثم يضم الشرب اليها وباعهما فيصرف الثمن الى ثمن الأرض والفاضل الى قضاء الدين
ترجمہ اور شرب کو بیچا نہیں جائے گا صاحب شرب کے قرض میں اس کی موت کے بعد بغیر زمین کے جیسا کہ اس کی زندگی میں اور امام کیسے کرے تو اصح یہ ہے کہ شرب کو ایسی زمین کی طرف ملادے جس کے لئے شرب نہ ہو پھر ان دونوں کو فروخت کر دے صاحب زمین کی اجازت سے پھر دیکھے زمین کی قیمت شرب کے ساتھ اور بغیر شرب کے پس تفاوت کو قرض ادا کرنے کی جانب صرف کیا جائے اور اگر امام ایسی زمین نہ پائے تو میت کے ترکہ کے اوپر بغیر شرب کی زمین خریدے پھر اس کی طرف شرب کو ملا دے اور ان دونوں کو فروخت کر دے پس ثمن کو زمین کے ثمن کی جانب صرف کیا جائے اور فاضل قرض ادا کرنے کی جانب
And shurb will not be sold for the debt of its owner after his death without land, just as during his lifetime. And what should the imam do? The most correct is that he annexes it to land that has no shurb, then sells both with the permission of the landowner, then looks at the price of the land with shurb and without it, then spends the difference to repay the debt. If he does not find that, he buys land without shurb from the deceased's estate, then annexes the shurb to it and sells both, then spends the price on the purchase price of the land, and the surplus to repay the debt.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage explains the practical procedure for dealing with shurb when the deceased has debts. Since shurb cannot be sold independently (as established earlier), the imam (ruler or judge) must employ one of two methods to realize its value. The first method: find another person's land that has no shurb, annex the deceased's shurb to that land with the owner's permission, sell the combination, and then divide the proceeds: the landowner gets the value of his land without shurb, and the deceased's shurb's value (the difference) goes to repay the debt. The second method: if no such land is available, the imam purchases a piece of land without shurb from the deceased's estate (i.e., using estate funds), annexes the shurb, sells the combined property, and then uses the sale proceeds to cover the purchase cost of the land first, then the remainder goes to the debt. This shows the Hanafi commitment to practical solutions while respecting the principle that shurb cannot be sold alone.

Key Terms
امام (imam): The ruler or judge authorized to oversee debt repayment and estate administration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what must the imam do first if the deceased has only a shurb and needs to repay his debt?
A) Sell the shurb alone.
B) Annex the shurb to someone else's land with permission and sell the combination.
C) Give the shurb to the creditor.
D) Wait for the shurb to increase in value.

Key Takeaway
Shurb must be sold with land to repay debt; the imam has two approved methods.

Shurb Cannot Be Sold Alone: The Hanafi Ruling and Two Remedial Methods
Ruling on not selling water rights for debt and two remedies by the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why shurb cannot be sold independently and explain the two methods by which the imam can facilitate its sale to pay off debt.

Core Idea
Shurb is a right, not property; it can only be sold when attached to land.

In this passage from Kitab Ihya al-Mawat, Al-Hidayah addresses a practical problem: a deceased person leaves only a water right (shurb) but owes debt. Can the imam sell the shurb alone? The answer is no—because shurb is a right (haqq), not a commodity (mal). However, the law provides two remedy methods to avoid injustice. Let's explore how the soundest opinion (asahh) solves this.

Guided Path
1
Extract the general ruling
State the prohibition: selling shurb alone to pay off debt is not permitted, just as it was not permitted during the owner's lifetime.
This is based on the principle that shurb is a right (haqq) attached to land, not independent property (mal).
2
Analyze the first remedy
The imam finds land without a water right, attaches the deceased's shurb to it with the landowner's permission, sells the combined property, and allocates the proceeds: the landowner receives the value of his land without shurb, and the difference goes to the debt.
Example from commentary: land without shurb worth 300, with shurb worth 500 → 300 to landowner, 200 to debt.
3
Analyze the second remedy
If no such land is available, the imam purchases a plot of land from the deceased's estate, attaches the shurb, sells both, uses the sale price to recover the purchase cost, and the surplus goes to the debt.
This ensures the sale is valid because shurb is now attached to land.
4
Compare the two remedies
Both remedies achieve a valid sale of shurb by pairing it with land. The first relies on a third party's land, the second uses estate funds to buy land.
The key condition is that shurb must never be sold in isolation.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Work through a numerical example: Debt is 400, land without shurb is 200, combined sale is 600. Using remedy 1, the landowner gets 200, debt gets 400. Using remedy 2, the imam buys land for 200, sells combined for 600, reimburses 200, pays 400 to debt.
Both yield the same net result for the creditors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب احياء الموات

صاحب شرب کے قرض میں شرب کو بیچا نہیں جائے گا

ولا يباع الشرب في دين صاحبه بعد موته بدون أرض كما في حال حياته وكيف يصنع الإمام الأصح أن يضم إلى أرض لا شرب لها فيبيعها بإذن صاحبها ثم ينظر إلى قسمة الأرض مع الشرب وبدونه فيصرف التفاوت إلى قضاء الدين وإن لم يجد ذلك اشترى على تركة الميت أرضا بغير شرب ثم يضم الشرب إليها وباعهما فيصرف الثمن إلى ثمن الأرض والفاضل إلى قضاء الدين

ترجمہ: اور شرب کو بیچا نہیں جائے گا صاحب شرب کے قرض میں اس کی موت کے بعد بغیر زمین کے جیسا کہ اس کی زندگی میں۔ اور امام کیسے کرے تو اصح یہ ہے کہ شرب کو ایسی زمین کی طرف ملادے جس کے لئے شرب نہ ہو پھر ان دونوں کو فروخت کر دے صاحب زمین کی اجازت سے پھر دیکھے زمین کی قیمت شرب کے ساتھ اور بغیر شرب کے پس تفاوت کو قرض ادا کرنے کی جانب صرف کیا جائے۔ اور اگر امام ایسی زمین نہ پائے تو میت کے ترکہ کے اوپر بغیر شرب کی زمین خریدے پھر اس کی طرف شرب کو ملا دے اور ان دونوں کو فروخت کر دے پس ثمن کو زمین کے ثمن کی جانب صرف کیا جائے اور فاضل قرض ادا کرنے کی جانب۔

تشریح: ماقبل میں بتایا جا چکا ہے کہ تنہا شرب کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر کوئی شخص مر جائے اور تنہا شرب چھوڑ کر مرے اور اس کے ذمہ قرض ہو تو شرب کی بیع اب بھی جائز نہیں تو اب امام کیا کرے اور کیسے قرض ادا ہو تو مصنف نے فرمایا کہ اس کی دو ترکیبیں ہیں۔
(1) اس کے برابر میں کسی کی ایسی زمین دیکھے جس کے لئے شرب نہ ہو اور امام اس شرب کو اس زمین سے ملادے اور زمین والے کی اجازت سے زمین کو مع شرب کے فروخت کر دے اب غور کیا جائے کہ بغیر شرب کے زمین کی کیا قیمت تھی اور شرب کے ساتھ کیا قیمت ہے مثلا شرب کے ساتھ زمین کی قیمت پانچ سو روپے ہیں اور بغیر شرب کے تین سو روپے تھی تو تین سو روپے زمین والے کے اور دو سو کو قرض ادا کرنے میں صرف کرے۔
(2) امام میت کے ترکہ پر کوئی ایسی زمین خریدے جس کے لئے شرب نہ ہو اور اس شرب کو اس زمین کے ساتھ ملادے پھر ان دونوں کو فروخت کر دے تو زمین کا ثمن وہاں دے جہاں سے زمین خریدنے کے لئے رقم اٹھائی ہے اور باقی سے میت کا قرضہ ادا کرے۔
And water right (shurb) shall not be sold for the debt of its owner after his death without land, just as in his lifetime. And how should the imam act? The soundest view is that he should attach it to land that has no water right, then sell both with the landowner's permission. Then he considers the division of the land with and without the water right, and applies the difference to discharge the debt. If he does not find such land, he purchases land without a water right from the deceased's estate, then attaches the water right to it, sells both, and applies the price to the price of the land and the surplus to discharge the debt.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on reviving dead lands (Ihya al-Mawat). The ruling is that a water right (shurb) cannot be sold separately from land to pay off the debt of a deceased person, just as it could not be sold separately during his lifetime. The reason is that shurb is a right (haqq) attached to land, not a standalone property. However, if the deceased leaves only a shurb and has debts, the imam (ruler or judge) must find a remedy. The text provides two approved methods (the 'asahh' or soundest opinion). First, the imam finds a piece of land that has no water right, attaches the deceased's shurb to it with the landowner's permission, sells the combined property, and distributes the proceeds: the landowner gets the value of his land without shurb, and the difference goes to the debt. Second, if no such land is available, the imam purchases a plot of land from the deceased's estate, attaches the shurb, sells both, and uses the sale price to recover the purchase cost and the remainder for the debt. The commentary clarifies that this is because a standalone sale of shurb is invalid, so the imam must combine it with land to effect a valid sale. This example illustrates the Hanafi principle that certain rights cannot be traded independently but may be transferred together with their subject matter.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): A legal right to draw water from a source (e.g., a canal or well) for irrigating land; it is a usufructuary right (haqq intifa') attached to land.
اصح (asahh): The soundest opinion within the Hanafi school on a particular issue, often chosen by the commentator (Al-Hidayah author) when there is intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to sell the shurb (water right) alone to pay off the deceased's debt?
A) Because the shurb is not owned by the deceased.
B) Because the shurb is a right (haqq) and not a property (mal), so it cannot be sold independently.
C) Because the imam does not have authority to sell the shurb.
D) Because the shurb is attached to the land and cannot be separated.

Key Takeaway
Shurb is a right, not property; its independent sale is batil, but it can be sold combined with land to settle debts.
